**Chapter 2**
develops finance technical reports, maintains a repository of reported data, and performs financial data
analytics for senior leader decision-making.
**Army Financial Management Center Teams**
2-27. There are three teams in the AFMC, each forward stationed and aligned with a TSC. The AFMC teams
and their capabilities are discussed in Section 3 of this chapter.

## UNIFIED ACTION PARTNERS

2-28. It is critical that the FM enterprise works with other agencies to achieve integrated whole-of-
government operations and synchronization of interagency activities, such as information sharing, security
cooperation, and foreign assistance. In order to ensure success across the range of military operations, U.S.
forces rely on unified action partners. Unified action partners are those military forces, governmental and
nongovernmental organizations, and elements of the private sector with whom Army forces plan, coordinate,
synchronize, and integrate during the conduct of operations (ADP 3-0). Synchronization, coordination, and
most importantly, cooperation must occur between the FM enterprise and unified action partners to employ
effective capabilities.

### OFFICE OF THEUNDERSECRETARY OFDEFENSE(COMPTROLLER)

2-29. The Under Secretary of Defense (Comptroller) (USD[C]) is the DOD chief financial officer and the
principal advisor to the Secretary of Defense for budgetary and fiscal matters including FM, accounting
policy and systems, management control systems, budget formulation and execution, contract and audit
administration, and general management improvement programs. The Office of the USD(C) establishes and
supervises the execution of principles, policies, and procedures relating to the preparation and execution of
DOD budgets that include fiscal, cost, operating, capital property accounting, and statistical reporting. It
establishes and supervises the execution of policies and procedures relating to the expenditure and collection
of funds administered by the DOD. Furthermore, it is responsible for informing each of the congressional
defense committees on all matters related to the budgetary, fiscal, and analytic DOD activities under the
supervision of the USD(C).

### DEFENSEFINANCE ANDACCOUNTINGSERVICE

2-30. DFAS is an agency supporting the Office of the USD(C) and is responsible for providing finance and
accounting services and monitoring compliance with all statutory and regulatory requirements. It manages
the consolidation, standardization, and integration of finance and accounting requirements, functions, and
procedures within the DOD. It coordinates and collaborates with all defense agencies, military departments,
and combatant commands to deliver accurate, timely, and relevant financial information and employs
enhanced technological capabilities that provide critical finance and accounting services to DOD customers
and stakeholders.
2-31. DFAS and other national providers issue guidance and provide support back at the home station or
within the area of operations that helps the commander maintain control and achieve accountability over
resources. DOD 7000.14-R, Volume 4 provides the policy and standards by which the component should
establish financial control over its assets. Financial control is a main objective of accounting and helps ensure
proper and authorized use of all assets as well as adequate care and preservation. It is also responsible for
executing statutory and regulatory financial reporting requirements and rendering financial statements.

### DEPARTMENT OFTREASURY

2-32. The Department of Treasury is the executive agency responsible for promoting the conditions that
enable economic growth and stability at home and abroad, strengthening national security by combating
threats and protecting the integrity of the financial system, and managing the Government’s finances and
resources effectively. It is responsible for a wide range of activities such as advising the President on
economic and financial issues, encouraging sustainable economic growth, and fostering improved
governance in financial institutions. It operates and maintains systems that are critical to the nation's financial
infrastructure, such as the production of coin and currency, the disbursement of payments to the American
public, revenue collection, and the borrowing of funds necessary to run the Federal Government. It works
**20**
**FM 4-80**
**21 April 2025**
**Financial Management at Echelon**
with other federal agencies, foreign governments, and international financial institutions to encourage global
economic growth, raise standards of living, and to the extent possible, predict and prevent economic and
financial crises. The Department of Treasury also performs a critical and far-reaching role in enhancing
national security by implementing economic sanctions against foreign threats to the U.S., identifying and
targeting the financial support networks of national security threats, and improving the safeguards of our
financial systems.

### FEDERALRESERVESYSTEM

2-33. The Federal Reserve System (often referred to as the Federal Reserve or simply “the Fed”) is the central
bank of the United States. It performs five general functions to promote the effective operation of the U.S.
economy and, more generally, the public interest. It conducts the nation's monetary policy, promotes the
stability of the financial system, promotes the safety and soundness of individual financial institutions, and
promotes consumer protection and community development. Additionally, the Federal Reserve fosters
payment and settlement system safety and efficiency through services to the banking industry and the U.S.
Government that facilitate U.S. dollar transactions and payments.
2-34. The 12 federal reserve banks comprise an element of the Federal Reserve System. One of the
responsibilities of the reserve banks is to provide key financial services that support the nation’s payment
system. These services include distributing the nation's currency and coin to depository institutions, clearing
checks, operating the FedWire and Automated Clearing House systems, and serving as a bank for the
Department of Treasury.

### DEFENSESECURITYCOOPERATIONAGENCY

2-35. The Defense Security Cooperation Agency (DSCA) mission is to advance U.S. defense and foreign
policy interests by building the capacity of foreign partners in order to encourage and enable allies and
partners to respond to shared challenges. DSCA leads the broader U.S. security cooperation enterprise in its
efforts to train, educate, advise, and equip foreign partners. DSCA oversees and administers security
cooperation programs that support U.S. policy interests and objectives identified by the President, DOD, and
DOS. These objectives include developing specific partner capabilities, building alliances and partnerships,
and facilitating U.S. access. DSCA integrates security cooperation activities in support of a whole-of-
government approach, provides execution guidance to DOD entities that implement security cooperation
programs, exercises financial and program management for the Foreign Military Sales System and many
other security cooperation programs, and educates and provides for the long-term development of the security
cooperation workforces.

### SECTION III – THEATER STRATEGIC LEVEL OF WARFARE

2-36. The theater strategic level of warfare is the level of warfare at which combatant commanders
synchronize with unified action partners and employ all elements of national power to fulfill policy aims
within the assigned theater in support of the national strategy (FM 3-0). Based on strategic guidance, CCDRs
with assigned areas of responsibility and staffs update their strategic estimates and develop theater strategies
with input from subordinate commands, including theater Armies and supporting commands and agencies.
A theater strategy is an overarching construct outlining a CCDR’s vision for integrating and synchronizing
military activities and operations with the other instruments of national power to achieve national strategic
objectives. The theater strategy prioritizes the ends, ways, and means within the limitations established by
the budget, global force management processes, and strategic guidance. The theater strategy serves as the
basis for development of the combatant command campaign plan.
2-37. The following paragraphs discuss Army FM capabilities at the theater strategic level of warfare.
Knowing the capabilities and organizational structure of FM elements at the theater strategic level of warfare
is essential to planning, preparing, executing, and assessing FM operations vital to provide procurement
support to the CCDR’s AOR. **Procurement support****is the critical role financial management plays in**
**acquiring, certifying, accounting, and disbursing the funding requirements for operational contract**
**support**.
2-38. Figure 2-5 on page 22 illustrates the FM organizations and command staff structures at the theater
strategic level of warfare.
**21 April 2025**
**FM 4-80**
**21**
**Chapter 2**
**Figure 2-5. Army FM organizations at the theater strategic level of warfare**

## THEATER ARMY

2-39. The theater Army's primary role is to serve as the ASCC to a combatant command, and its mission is
the most diverse and complex of any Army echelon. The theater Army headquarters is tailored to a specific
combatant command with the ability to conduct both operational and administrative C2 over Army forces
theater wide. It provides enabling capabilities appropriate to theater conditions such as intelligence,
sustainment, signal, fires, information activities, civil affairs, engineer, and medical. In theaters without
assigned field armies, corps, or divisions, the theater Army assumes direct responsibility across warfighting
functions for its tactical commands. See FM 3-94 and ATP 3-93 for additional information on the theater
Army.
2-40. The theater Army performs seven functions as the ASCC:
•
Execute the CCDR's daily operational requirements.
•
Provide administrative control of Army forces.
•
Set and maintain the theater.
•
Set and support operational areas.
•
Exercise C2 of Army forces in the theater.
•
Perform joint roles of limited scope, scale, and duration.
•
Plan and coordinate for the consolidation of gains in support of joint operations.
2-41. The theater Army G-8 is the principal staff office responsible for resourcing requirements to facilitate
theater-level operations. It performs and oversees audit readiness, management internal controls, and
accounting functions. It coordinates and establishes FM guidance and policies, to include the types of funds
authorized in the supplemental and other appropriations, fund sites, and funding levels for tactical commands.
**22**
**FM 4-80**
**21 April 2025**
**Financial Management at Echelon**
The theater Army G-8 manages the PPBE process and determines sources of funding for validated
requirements.
2-42. The theater Army G-8 coordinates, synchronizes, and validates funds for requirements and ensures the
fiscal planning is incorporated into theater planning. The Secretary of Defense or Deputy Secretary of
Defense may designate the Army as the executive agent for an operation. In these cases, the theater Army
provides the funding for common-level support to all DOD participants.
2-43. Theater Army G-8 functions include—
•
Identifying sources of funds, receiving funding, and distributing and controlling funds to
subordinate units.
•
Tracking costs and obligations.
•
Providing accounting support.
•
Establishing and implementing internal controls.
•
Interpreting, advising on, and monitoring compliance with RM guidance, directives, policies,
regulations, and laws.
•
Coordinating and establishing fiscal policy and guidance through the orders process.
•
Contributing to annexes, running estimates, orders, and the concept of support.

## THEATER SUSTAINMENT COMMAND

2-44. The TSC is the Army's command for the integration and synchronization of sustainment in the
combatant command AOR. The TSC integrates strategic enablers at the operational level. The TSC is
assigned to an ASCC and provides Title 10 support for Army forces. The TSC manages requirements for
sustainment and the physical flow of forces, equipment, and cargo to meet the daily operational requirements
of the ASCC. The command ensures the information flow from strategic deployment, distribution, and
sustainment partners is accurate, timely, and adequate to support the actions of theater sustainment forces.
For additional information on the TSC see ATP 4-93.
2-45. The TSC has four operational responsibilities to forces in theater:
•
Theater opening.
•
Theater distribution.
•
Sustainment.
•
Theater closing.

### THEATERSUSTAINMENTCOMMANDG-8

2-46. The TSC G-8 is the principal staff officer responsible for all RM functions in support of the TSC
commander's priorities, as well as funding for assigned forces. The G-8 coordinates, synchronizes, and funds
validated requirements by identifying the appropriate source of funds. The TSC G-8’s primary
responsibilities are providing advice and guidance concerning funding decisions and ensuring that adequate
funding sources are available for the TSC commander, the TSC staff, and subordinate units.
2-47. The TSC G-8 maintains a close relationship with contracting support brigades, legal units, and finance
units due to their critical role in operational contract support. The G-8 coordinates with contracting support
to ensure legality, prompt payment, and reconciliation of contract payments to identify unused funds. It is
critical to maintain fiscal stewardship and utilize internal control measures to avoid any illegal use of funds
and authorities.
2-48. The TSC G-8 functions include—
•
Identifying sources of funds, receiving funding, and distributing and controlling funds to
subordinate units.
•
Tracking costs and obligations.
•
Providing accounting support.
•
Establishing and implementing internal controls.
•
Contributing to annexes, running estimates, orders, and the concept of support.
**21 April 2025**
**FM 4-80**
**23**
**Chapter 2**

### FINANCEOPERATIONSCENTER

2-49. The FIOC is a theater-level staff element assigned to the distribution management center of a TSC. The
FIOC serves as the primary finance integrator for current operations, future operations, and future plans. It
provides finance synchronization by recommending to the commander optimized employment, integration,
direction, and control of finance elements. The FIOC is responsible for coordinating finance support between
the finance battalions (FIBNs), finance support center (FISC), and the AFMC team. It is the primary liaison
between theater finance elements and the AFMC headquarters responsible for coordinating the publication
of orders and policy with higher headquarters.
2-50. FIOC functions include—
•
Providing a finance planning capability to the TSC distribution management center for current
operations, future operations, and future plans.
•
Anticipating requirements for obtaining, storing, and transporting physical currency and finance
systems.
•
Synchronizing, coordinating, and assessing finance operations and requirements throughout the
theater.
•
Identifying finance force structure requirements and recommending allocation and emplacement of
finance units in theater.
•
Preparing finance annexes, running estimates, orders, and the concept of support.
•
Managing theater finance operations reporting requirements.
•
Coordinating theater finance policy.

### ARMYFINANCIALMANAGEMENTCENTERTEAM

2-51. The AFMC team is USAFMCOM's operational element for conducting contingency or establishing
theater finance operations. It is forward stationed and aligned with the TSC until the arrival of the FISC. The
AFMC team is responsible for central funding, overseeing internal controls, and providing finance systems
support across the theater. Upon arrival of the FISC, the AFMC team can provide the FISC with augmentation
to ensure continuity of operations and provide operational flexibility in the form of increased capacity.
2-52. The functions of the AFMC team include—
•
Providing theater disbursing support through central funding.
•
Advising and assisting with establishing and maintaining a DSSN.
•
Advising commanders on local banking infrastructure and the establishment of limited depositary
accounts (LDAs).
•
Establishing and overseeing internal controls for theater finance units.
•
Interpreting, advising on, and monitoring compliance with finance guidance, directives, policies,
regulations, and laws.
•
Establishing, coordinating, and maintaining finance systems.
•
Negotiating HN banking agreements.
**Disbursing Section**
2-53. The AFMC team disbursing section is responsible for theater central funding. It coordinates with HN
support and military banking operations to establish and sustain the flow of currency (local or U.S.) to the
FIBNs, other DOD agencies, Services, and multinational forces in accordance with inter-service and
intergovernmental agreements. The disbursing section maintains a DSSN and may be designated to provide
currency to all components of a joint or multinational force. This section also coordinates with the DOS, local
U.S. embassy, DFAS, and the Department of Treasury to establish HN banking support requirements. The
disbursing section is the Department of Treasury account holder for the central funding account and
coordinates the selection of any limited depositary institutions in theater. The banking team facilitates the
analysis of HN financial institutions for LDAs and for the establishment of local banks on DOD installations.
The section obtains support and policy decisions from an Army banking officer.
**24**
**FM 4-80**
**21 April 2025**
**Financial Management at Echelon**
**Internal Control Section**
2-54. The AFMC internal control team assists commanders in evaluating finance units on their adherence to
standard business processes, accountability control effectiveness, and compliance with applicable
regulations, legislative directives, theater finance policy, and management controls. It provides commanders
with advice regarding the interpretation and dissemination of finance directives, policy, and guidance
developed by FM enterprise unified action partners.
**Finance Systems Section**
2-55. The finance systems section facilitates financial management information system (FMIS) utilization
and knowledge management procedures to collect, process, store, display, disseminate, and protect data and
information. This section coordinates and provides software updates and hardware replacement; configures
and troubleshoots local area networks and routers; disseminates and enforces signal policies; installs,
operates, maintains, and performs limited maintenance on network computing equipment (for example,
routers, switches, and computers); and performs cyber security functions.

### FINANCESUPPORTCENTER

2-56. The FISC is a Reserve Component staff element responsible for central funding, overseeing internal
controls, technical oversight, and providing finance systems support across the theater. It provides support
for theater policy development and the synchronization and integration of finance operations. It receives
request for support through the FIOC from the FIBN or expeditionary sustainment command (ESC). The rule
of allocation is one FISC per TSC. The FISC operates under the operational control of the TSC and or ESC,
and the director serves as the principal FM advisor to the TSC/ESC commander.
2-57. FISC functions include the following:
•
Providing theater disbursing support through central funding.
•
Advising and assisting with establishing and maintaining a DSSN.
•
Providing technical oversight.
•
Establishing and implementing internal controls for theater finance units.
•
Interpreting, advising on, and monitoring compliance with finance guidance, directives, policies,
regulations, and laws.
•
Establishing, coordinating, and maintaining finance systems.
**Organization Structure**
2-58. The sections within the FISC headquarters include plans and operations, finance operations, disbursing,
internal control, policy and finance systems. Figure 2-6 depicts the organization of the FISC.
**Figure 2-6. Finance support center**
**Plans and Operations Section**
2-59. The plans and operations section coordinates the overall operation and readiness posture of the FISC
in theater.

**Finance Operations Section**
2-60. The finance operations section supports the FIOC in integration and synchronization of current
operations, future operations, and future plans. It conducts financial preparation of the environment in close
coordination with unified action partners.
**Disbursing Section**
2-61. The disbursing section is responsible for theater central funding. It coordinates with HN support and
military banking operations to establish and sustain the flow of currency (local or U.S.) to the FIBNs, other
DOD agencies, Services, and multinational forces in accordance with inter-service and intergovernmental
agreements. The disbursing section maintains a DSSN and may be designated to provide currency to all
components of a joint or multinational force. Through the FIOC, this section also coordinates with
USAFMCOM, DOS, local U.S. embassies, DFAS, and the Treasury to establish HN banking support
requirements. The disbursing section is the Department of Treasury account holder for the central funding
account and coordinates the selection of any limited depositary institutions in theater. The banking team
facilitates the analysis of HN financial institutions for LDAs and for the establishment of local banks on DOD
installations. The section obtains support and policy decisions from an Army banking officer.
**Internal Control Section**
2-62. The internal control section provides the TSC commander the capability to evaluate finance units on
their adherence to standard business processes, accountability control effectiveness, and compliance with
applicable regulations, legislative directives, and management controls.
**Policy Section**
2-63. The policy section assists the theater Army G-8 in developing, recommending, and coordinating theater
finance policy. It provides commanders with advice regarding the interpretation and dissemination of finance
directives, policy, and guidance.
**Finance Systems Section**
2-64. The finance systems section facilitates FMIS utilization and knowledge management procedures to
collect, process, store, display, disseminate, and protect data and information. This section coordinates and
provides software updates and hardware replacement; configures and troubleshoots local area networks and
routers; disseminates and enforces signal policies; installs, operates, maintains, and performs limited
maintenance on network computing equipment (for example, routers, switches, and computers); and
performs cyber security functions.

## EXPEDITIONARY SUSTAINMENT COMMAND

2-65. At the theater echelon, one or more ESCs can be attached to a TSC. The ESC is attached to a TSC and
provides C2 over all assigned and attached units in an operational area as directed by the TSC. The ESC is
capable of planning, coordinating, integrating, and synchronizing sustainment in support of Army forces and,
when directed, joint and multi-national forces. It may perform the function of a forward command post for
the TSC. The ESC is dependent on the TSC staff for long-range planning and enabling capabilities.
2-66. The ESC may form the nucleus of an expeditionary joint command for logistics when provided with
joint force augmentation. The ESC performing as a joint command for logistics will normally locate within
a joint area of operations while another ESC or sustainment brigade assumes the responsibilities for
supporting Army forces. For more information on the ESC, see ATP 4-92.

### EXPEDITIONARYSUSTAINMENTCOMMANDG-8

2-67. ESC G-8s are the principal staff officers responsible for all RM functions in support of ESC commander
priorities. They coordinate, synchronize, and fund validated requirements by identifying the appropriate
source of funds. They provide advice and guidance to the commander concerning resources and ensure
adequate funding sources are available.
**26**
**FM 4-80**
**21 April 2025**
**Financial Management at Echelon**
2-68. The ESC G-8 has a critical role in operational contract support and maintains a close relationship with
the contracting support brigade. The G-8 coordinates contracting support to ensure legality, prompt payment,
and reconciliation of contract payments to identify unused funds.
2-69. The ESC G-8 functions include—
•
Identifying sources of funds, receiving funding, and distributing and controlling funds to
subordinate units.
•
Tracking costs and obligations.
•
Providing accounting support.
•
Establishing and implementing internal controls.
•
Contributing to annexes, running estimates, orders, and concepts of support in coordination with the
TSC G-8 or corps G-8 and FIBNs.

### EXPEDITIONARYSUSTAINMENTCOMMANDFINANCEOPERATIONSBRANCH

2-70. The ESC finance operations branch is in the ESC distribution management center. It is responsible for
coordinating central funding, internal controls, and finance systems support between the FIBN, FIOC, and
higher headquarters. The finance support operations officer within the finance operations branch is the
principal staff officer for planning, coordinating, and synchronizing external finance operations for the ESC.
2-71. The finance operations branch functions include—
•
Synchronizing, coordinating, and integrating all finance operations within the area of operations.
•
Coordinating the acquisition, storing, and transportation of physical currency.
•
Advising on the employment of finance units.
•
Contributing to the preparation of finance annexes, running estimates, and the concept of support.

### THEATERFINANCEBATTALION

2-72. The theater finance battalion (T-FIBN) is a Reserve Component organization. Its primary focus is
finance from the national strategic to theater strategic levels of war. It is assigned to an ESC and provides
general support in the theater strategic level of war. The T-FIBN provides C2 of subordinate theater finance
companies (T-FICOs); oversees assigned unit readiness; synchronizes operations for assigned units; provides
limited administrative and supply support for assigned units; manages and provides disbursing service
support; enforces internal controls; and provides limited FMIS support. The rule of allocation for the T-FIBN
is one per two-six T-FICOs.
2-73. The T-FIBN commander is a primary account holder to the Department of Treasury and is responsible
for determining currency requirements (U.S. and foreign), funding subordinate finance companies (FICOs),
and obtaining additional currency as needed. Upon orders, the T-FIBN can be used as a general support-
reinforcing unit in support of a corps area of operations.
2-74. The T-FIBN's functions include the following:
•
Providing disbursing support and oversight to subordinate FICOs.
•
Providing payment support for assigned area of operations.
•
Providing internal control assistance and enforcement for subordinate FICOs.
•
Providing C2 of subordinate FICOs.
2-75. The T-FIBN is comprised of a headquarters and headquarters detachment, personnel/logistics section
(S-1/S-4), operations section (S-3), signal section (S-6), internal control section, and disbursing section.
Figure 2-7 on page 28 depicts the organization of the T-FIBN headquarters.

**Theater Finance Battalion Headquarters**
2-76. The command group is organized and equipped to suit the commander's decision making and leadership
requirements, while enabling the commander to accomplish critical C2 of battalion formations assigned and
attached. It provides planning, technical guidance, and supports subordinate T-FICOs conducting operations
in theater.
**Headquarters and Headquarters Detachment**
2-77. The headquarters and headquarters detachment, while not a staff section, provides C2, administrative,
and logistics support for T-FIBN personnel. It organizes the day-to-day mission in coordination with the
headquarters and the other sections.
**S-1/S-4 Section**
2-78. The S-1/S-4 section provides personnel and administrative support and limited postal services to the
battalion and subordinate companies. It manages personnel strengths and actions for all subordinate units,
including personnel readiness. It provides the full range of logistics support from property accountability to
maintenance. The section oversees the battalion's property book and equipment readiness to include
coordinating with external logistics support agencies for repairs, upgrades, and modifications.
**S-3/Support Operations Section**
2-79. The S-3/Support Operations section is the focal point for task organization, planning, operations, and
training. It coordinates the personnel security program. This section is responsible for planning, coordinating,
integrating, and synchronizing finance operations with the finance operations branch of the ESC distribution
management center.
**S-6 Section**
2-80. The S-6 section provides staff planning and supervision of communications for the battalion. It provides
for the installation, operation, and maintenance of battalion internal signal communications and electronic
equipment. It conducts network operations to establish, operate, manage, protect, and defend
communications networks and information services. The section manages organic communications
capabilities and computers, and coordinates for the use of external communications capabilities based on
mission variables. It provides and coordinates limited support for FMIS software and hardware updates.

**Internal Control Section**
2-81. The internal control section provides the commander the capability to evaluate finance units on their
adherence to standard business processes, accountability control effectiveness, and compliance with
applicable regulations, legislative directives, theater finance policy, and management controls. This section
provides evaluations of assigned finance units' technical proficiency. It may be augmented as required by the
internal control section within the FISC to provide a more detailed and robust capability, depending on the
mission.
**Disbursing Section**
2-82. The disbursing section establishes and maintains a contingency DSSN; establishes, maintains, and
manages LDAs; makes payments on properly prepared and certified vouchers; receives, controls, issues, and
safeguards all currencies; cashes negotiable instruments; receives collections; and makes foreign currency
conversions. It maintains accountable records and conducts reconciliation of financial transactions. This
section has responsibility for funding subordinate FICOs and for determining the need for currencies and
their replenishment across its area of operations.
**Theater Finance Company**
2-83. The T-FICO only exists in the Reserve Component. The T-FICO is typically under the C2 of the
T-FIBN and provides general support to its assigned area of operations. The T-FICO has a disbursing section
and four organic finance support teams (FSTs) capable of operating independently to support sustainment
brigades, contingency contracting teams, and other finance operations. Upon orders, the T-FICO may be
tasked organized as either a general support or a general support-reinforcing unit in support of a corps area
of operations. The rule of allocation for the T-FICO is one per ESC, two per sustainment brigade, and one
per contracting support brigade. Figure 2-8 depicts the organization of the T-FICO.
2-84. The T-FICO's functions include the following:
•
Providing disbursing support.
•
Providing payment support for assigned area of operations.

**Disbursing Section**
2-85. The disbursing section makes payments on properly prepared and certified vouchers; receives, controls,
issues, and safeguards all currencies; cashes negotiable instruments; receives collections; and makes foreign
currency conversions. It maintains accountable records and conducts reconciliation of financial transactions.
This section has responsibility for funding FSTs.
2-86. The disbursing section also has commercial vendor services personnel that receive and review
documents (new contracts, modifications, invoices, and receiving reports) for accuracy using document
control procedures. They process, calculate, prepare, verify, and certify payments of contracts, while ensuring

legality and prompt payment. They work closely with contracting and the resource manager to coordinate
contracting support and to ensure the legality, prompt payment, and reconciliation of contract payments.
**Finance Support Teams**
2-87. The FST provides disbursing and pay support to all units and Soldiers in its area of operations. When
mission variables dictate, the team can be augmented with additional support from the T-FICO. All
accountable items are cleared through the disbursing section of the T-FICO.

### SECTION IV – OPERATIONAL LEVEL OF WARFARE

2-88. The operational level of warfare is the level of warfare in which campaigns and operations are planned,
conducted, and sustained to achieve operational objectives to support achievement of strategic objectives
(JP 3-0). The operational level links the employment of tactical forces to the achievement of strategic
objectives.
2-89. The operational level of warfare generally is the realm of combatant commands and their Service or
functional components, and subordinate joint task force (JTF) headquarters and their Service or functional
components. This includes the theater Army headquarters as the Army Service component to a combatant
command and any other echelon operating as an ARFOR, JTF headquarters, or land component command.
2-90. Actions at the operational level of warfare usually involve broader aspects of time and space than
tactical actions. Operational-level commanders need to understand the complexities of the OE and look
beyond the immediate situation. Operational-level commanders seek to create the most favorable conditions
possible for subordinate commanders by preparing for future events.
2-91. The following paragraphs discuss FM at the operational level of warfare. Knowing the capabilities and
organizational structure of FM elements at the operational level of warfare is essential to planning, preparing,
executing, and assessing FM operations.
2-92. Figure 2-9 illustrates the FM organizations and command staff structures at the operational level of
warfare.
**30**
**FM 4-80**
**21 April 2025**
**Financial Management at Echelon**
**Figure 2-9. Army FM organizations at the operational level of warfare**

## FIELD ARMY

2-93. A field army is an echelon of command that employs multiple corps, divisions, multifunctional
brigades, and functional brigades to achieve objectives on land (JP 3-31). The field army is the only echelon
above the brigade that is only a headquarters. Large-scale combat operations involving multiple corps may
require the establishment of a field army to function as the senior tactical or operational-level command
exercising C2 over multiple corps-sized formations. The field army's primary role is to serve as the ARFOR
or joint force land component command for multi-corps operations. When serving as the joint force land
component command, field armies require significant augmentation from the joint and multinational force.
Field armies are most likely to be employed in theaters where peer and near-peer adversaries have the
capability of conducting large-scale ground combat. Field armies possess no standardized force structure.
The Army tailors each field army to the conditions prevailing in its assigned area of operations. The field
army receives capabilities and units from external sources based on its requirements. See FM 3-94 and ATP
4-92 for additional information on field armies.
2-94. The field army G-8 executes all RM functions as the senior Army headquarters in its assigned area of
operations. Priorities of funding during competition, crisis, and armed conflict are a subset of theater Army
activities with a more limited scope and duration. The field army G-8 coordinates, synchronizes, and funds
validated resource requirements, identifies the appropriate source of funds, and provides the commander with
mission essential funding and solutions to ensure operational success.
2-95. Field army G-8 functions include—
•
Identifying sources of funds, receiving funding, and distributing and controlling funds to
subordinate units.
•
Tracking costs and obligations.
**21 April 2025**
**FM 4-80**
**31**
**Chapter 2**
•
Providing accounting support.
•
Establishing and implementing internal controls.
•
Contributing to annexes, running estimates, orders, and the concept of support.

## CORPS

2-96. The corps is able to operate at both the tactical and operational levels. While it is organized, staffed,
trained, and equipped to fight as a tactical formation, the corps may be called upon to become a joint or
multinational headquarters for conducting operations. When operating as the senior Army headquarters under
a JTF, the corps will serve as the ARFOR. The corps can also serve as the coalition forces land component
commander (CFLCC) when properly augmented with joint and multinational personnel. If the corps is
uncommitted to specific CCDR requirements, it focuses on building and sustaining readiness to prevail in
large-scale combat operations. The roles of the corps include acting as the—
•
Senior Army tactical formation in large-scale combat, commanding two to five Army divisions
together with supporting brigades and commands.
•
ARFOR (with augmentation) within a joint force for campaigns and major operations when a field
army is not present.
•
JTF headquarters (with significant augmentation) for crisis response and limited contingency
operations.
•
CFLCC (with significant augmentation) commanding Army, Marine Corps, and multinational
divisions together with supporting brigades and commands when a field army is not present.
2-97. During large-scale combat operations, a corps headquarters normally functions as a tactical
headquarters under a joint or multinational land component. The corps is the echelon best positioned and
resourced to achieve convergence with Army and joint capabilities. (See FM 3-94 and ATP 3-92 for more
information about Army corps.)
2-98. The corps sustainment command is the sustainment command assigned to the corps. The corps
sustainment command finance operations branch and G-8 are discussed in section 3 of this chapter.

### CORPSG-8

2-99. The corps G-8 is the principal staff officer responsible for all RM functions in support of the corps
commander's priorities, as well as funding for assigned forces. The G-8 staff coordinates, synchronizes, and
funds validated requirements and identifies the appropriate funding sources. The corps G-8 primary
responsibilities are providing advice and guidance concerning resources and ensuring that adequate funding
sources are available for the corps commander, the corps staff, and subordinate units.
2-100. The corps G-8 staff has a critical role in operational contract support and maintains a close relationship
with the contracting support brigade. The G-8 coordinates contracting support to ensure legality, prompt
payment, and reconciliation of contract payments.
2-101. The corps G-8 functions include—
•
Identifying sources of funds, receiving funding, and distributing and controlling funds to
subordinate units.
•
Tracking costs and obligations.
•
Providing accounting support.
•
Establishing and implementing internal controls.
•
Contributing to annexes, running estimates, orders, and the concept of support.

### CORPSFINANCEBATTALION

2-102. The corps finance battalion (C-FIBN) only exists in the Regular Army. The C-FIBN's primary focus
is on FM operations from the corps support area forward. It is assigned to a corps sustainment command and
provides general support in the corps support area. The C-FIBN provides C2 of subordinate corps finance
companies (C-FICOs); oversees assigned unit readiness; synchronizes operations for assigned units; provides
administrative and supply support for assigned units; manages and provides disbursing services and
commercial vendor services support; enforces internal controls; and provides limited FMIS support. The rule
of allocation for the C-FIBN is one per two-six C-FICOs.

contract payments.
**Early Entry Team**
2-115. The early entry team supports commanders as an advance party for a larger follow-on force, or to
conduct domestic operations such as disaster relief or humanitarian assistance. It possesses the capability to
execute finance operations autonomously until the arrival of the remainder of the C-FIBN.
**Corps Finance Company**
2-116. The C-FICO only exists in the Regular Army. The C-FICO is assigned under the C2 of the C-FIBN
and provides general support to its assigned area of operations. C-FICOs provide timely and accurate
payments in support of procurement and disbursing operations. The C-FICO has two organic finance platoons
that can operate independently and autonomously over significant time and distance to support contingencies
and other critical operations. Each finance platoon consists of four FSTs, capable of providing disbursing
