**Unit Commander's Finance Report**
3-94. The Unit Commander's Finance Report is issued to unit commanders on a monthly basis. This report
provides a one-line rollup of each Soldier's pay account and status. Unit commanders must review the report
and annotate, update, change, correct, add, or delete information as necessary, providing additional and
necessary documentation as required. The unit should maintain a copy of the report for its records and return
the certified copy to finance in accordance with its established procedures, but not later than ten days of
issuance and receipt.
**Daily Register of Transactions**
3-95. The Daily Register of Transactions provides information to the finance units on the actions taken on
the requests submitted. It gives the unit a record of transactions pertaining to assigned Soldiers. The report
consists of transactions that are processed, rejected, or recycled and is available each time the FMIS updates.
**Merged Accountability and Fund Reporting Reconciliation**
3-96. The MAFR is one of the most important tools used to track all cash payments. It verifies that payments
have been processed through the Master Military Pay Account System. The report provides a list of all
payments, canceled or returned checks, and cash collections by specific accounting and disbursing station
number (commonly known as ADSN) or DSSN.
3-97. The Specific Check of Unmatched Transactions Report does not replace the MAFR for active
component military pay operations at the field level but is designed to be used as a tool to aid reconciliation
of uncollected payments. It is a tool to effectively reduce the number of uncollected payments made within
the theater of operation and other non-integrated disbursing offices. It is not intended to eliminate MAFR
reconciling or balancing requirements, but rather to work in conjunction with the MAFR to give commanders
Reserve Component Pay.
3-98. Reserve Soldiers serve under a statutory or contractual obligation and are mobilized under Title 10
USC. The Defense Joint Military Pay System (DJMS)-Reserve Component is the system used to pay Ready
Reserve Soldiers for weekend training, annual training, and all other periods of active duty to include
mobilization. Unlike DJMS for the Active Component, some type of transaction must be input in order for
the system to generate pay. This system does not support allotments of pay. There are multiple pay dates (up
to eight possible) each month. Each payment generates a separate leave and earnings statement that contains
the information that applies to the specific payment. Unlike DJMS for the Active Component, the end-of-
month leave and earnings statement is not a summary statement for the month. Under mobilization, there will
typically be a mid-month and end-of-month leave and earnings statement generated for the 1st and 15th pay
dates. If a new entitlement begins, or a one-time payment or adjustment is entered for a pay date other than
the 1st or 15th of the month, there will be another statement generated for that payment alone.
**21 April 2025**
**FM 4-80**
**55**
**Chapter 3**
**Reserve Home Station Military Pay Processing**
3-99. Units conduct a Soldier Readiness Processing check for each Soldier mobilized from their unit at home
station. During the Soldier Readiness Process, Reserve Component Soldiers will be in-processed onto active
duty. One station will have finance personnel review the pay account and ensure entitlements are being
properly paid based upon the Soldier's supporting documentation.
3-100. On mobilization day, prior to movement to the mobilization station and during home station activities,
the U.S. Property and Fiscal Office of the affiliated state will start pay and entitlements. Soldiers continue
in-processing at the mobilization station as finance records are reviewed again by finance personnel with
adjustments or corrections being made as necessary. The pay account is checked to make sure the U.S. Army
Reserve Pay Center has started all entitlements, and for the Army National Guard, their state-affiliated U.S.
Property and Fiscal Office will start their pay and entitlements. If it is determined that the Soldier will not
deploy, the mobilization order must be rescinded or a new order releasing the Soldier from active duty must
be generated to stop payment of active duty pay.
**Deployment Site**
3-101. The deployment site is where Reserve Component Soldiers perform their mission, and they may move
to more than one deployment site while mobilized. While at the deployment site, if there is any pay problem,
a representative from the unit S-1 will contact the FICO on site. The FICO is responsible for monitoring
Reserve Component Soldier pay to ensure all authorized entitlements are paid in a timely manner, to include
theater-specific entitlements.
**Demobilization Pay Processing**
3-102. Reserve Component Soldiers will be released from active duty and reassessed back into a reserve
status, as appropriate, at the demobilization station. The Soldier's pay account will be reviewed for accuracy,
and any required adjustments will be made. Any unresolved pay problem should be resolved at this time.

### CASEMANAGEMENTSYSTEM

3-103. CMS provides an all-service, fully integrated, single-source system for monitoring pay problems,
uploading and tracking cases at all levels, and providing visibility at all levels for immediate feedback to
Service members. It provides timely and efficient identification of problem trends and focused training. It
provides supervisors oversight for prioritizing and identifying cases that require attention and provides
consolidated reporting capability for all organizational levels. CMS provides the capability for finance, in
coordination with DFAS, to work cases and identify trends to assist in applying resources and training
appropriately. Additional information on CMS may be found in the latest DFAS Case Management System
User's Guide.
3-104. CMS accepts manual input from the user and system-generated cases from a DJMS interface. There
are two types of CMS cases:
•
System Generated Cases. These are cases that are created from rejected transactions that pass
through the Automated Case Control System tables in DJMS and interfaced into CMS. The majority
of these cases will be “Opened”, “Action Completed” or “Closed” at the DFAS or local level.
•
Manual Cases. Manual cases are created by the finance system user for cases that cannot be
corrected on site.
3-105. FICOs are encouraged to institute personnel/pay teams that meet periodically to review problem cases
and identify solutions. CMS provides data for managers of all organizations responsible for action, which
allows oversight on the resolution of problem cases within their command. Managers have access to a wide
variety of reports that can be used to prioritize, manage timeliness, and develop training for recurring problem
types.
3-106. CMS embeds the processing timeline established by DFAS—30 days from the day the case was
initiated until the day the case is resolved. Cases are identified as overdue when they exceed 30 days. Cases
will show as “overdue” in the inbox of the organization responsible for action 5 days prior to the 30-day time
limit in order to provide early warning that the case needs to be worked.
**56**
**FM 4-80**
**21 April 2025**
**Finance Operations**

## TRAVEL PAY

3-107. Travel pay calculates, reviews, and processes travel allowances and reimbursements due to U.S. and
foreign personnel. Travel pay includes processing temporary duty, temporary change of station, and
permanent change of station travel orders. Finance personnel ensure accuracy and timeliness of payments to
reduce hardship and allow Soldiers to focus on operational requirements.
3-108. Finance units provide travel pay support for personnel assigned to the area of operations engaged in
official travel orders. Travel allowances can be paid by using a field expedient system such as the Integrated
Automated Travel System, which provides automated travel support. The Defense Travel System also
provides an additional platform to execute travel requirements.

### INVITATIONALTRAVELORDERS

3-109. During theater operations, organizations may process invitational travel orders. An invitational travel
order is used to reimburse certain travel and transportation expenses of an individual who is not a Service
member or civilian employee. Invitational travel orders must be issued judiciously to ensure prudent, proper,
and ethical use of appropriated funds. Individuals on invitational travel orders must be legitimately
performing a direct service for the government.

### TEMPORARYDUTYTRAVEL

3-110. The requirement for travel support to deployed personnel can be immense. In theater, per diem is
limited to incidental expenses only. During the competition and early stages of crisis and conflict, there may
be extensive requirements for temporary duty to and from the area of operations. Travel support also includes
noncombatant evacuation operation travel advances to noncombatants when they evacuate from the area of
operations (emergency evacuation allowances). The DOS may issue a noncombatant evacuation order for
U.S. citizens in the HN or target country. Evacuation payments are authorized under noncombatant
evacuation operation conditions and are usually paid outside the target country at a pre-designated safe haven.

### SECTION V – ACCOUNTING

3-111. The Army relies on the finance community to ensure fiscal stewardship of the public funds entrusted
to execute its assigned missions. Finance meets this expectation by providing expert fiscal analysis based on
timely and accurate financial data and accounting support.
3-112. Accounting support entails execution of all three types of accounting in the provision of theater FM
support to theater operations. Managerial cost accounting is the process of accumulating, measuring,
analyzing, interpreting, and reporting cost information useful to both internal and external groups concerned
with the way in which the organization uses, accounts for, safeguards, and controls its resources to meet its
objectives. Budgetary accounting is the accounting necessary to support and control the budget execution
process as distinguished from that required to report on financial conditions and operations (proprietary
accounting). For example, this includes commitments, obligations, expenditures, and conditions such as
appropriations realized, contract authority, and anticipated reimbursements. In contrast to budgetary
accounting, proprietary accounting involves those accounting functions and operations necessary to report
on financial conditions and financial results of an activity's operations. Proprietary accounting may include
accounting for inventory, accounts receivable, accounts payable, and accrued expenditures Details on the
particular procedures and processes related to federal budgetary, proprietary, and managerial cost accounting
are described in DOD 7000.14-R, Volume 1 and published Statement of Federal Financial Accounting
Standards.

## OVERVIEW OF ACCOUNTING ACTIVITIES

3-113. **Accounting support****is the accurate and complete recording of financial transactions within the**
**Army financial management information systems and the review and reconciliation of these financial**
**transactions to ensure the proper expenditure of entrusted funds in support of operations**. Accounting
facilitates establishing financial control, from time of acquisition to time of disposal, over all assets provided
to or acquired by commanders in support of operations. Additionally, accounting support provides the
requisite information to financial managers and commanders at all levels of the Army, strategic to tactical.
**21 April 2025**
**FM 4-80**
**57**
**Chapter 3**
Accounting support reinforces internal control over USG funds, collections, expenditures, property, and other
assets. Accounting in finance operations includes, but is not limited to, the critical activities of transaction
recording, transaction reconciliation, financial statements, and cost capturing.

## STANDARD LINE OF ACCOUNTING

3-114. All business events and financial events resulting in a commitment must cite a standard line of
accounting in accordance with DOD 7000.14-R, Volume 1. They must also be recorded in the general ledger
in accordance with the United States Standard General Ledger, Standard Financial Information Structure,
and Transaction Library.
3-115. The Standard Line of Accounting is a series of alpha and numeric characters appearing on accounting
source documents and is a subset of the Standard Financial Information Structure data standard elements.
Also referred to as the accounting classification code, it is comprised of the minimum Standard Financial
Information Structure data elements that must be exchanged for business events that have an accounting
impact at any point from the initial commitment to the final posting in the appropriate general ledger. A **line**
**of accounting****is a data structure representing a Department of Defense account that may be used to**
**track travel funding (transportation, per diem, meals, and incidental expenses) associated with an**
**organization's budget and to ensure accurate accounting transactions**. This includes commitments,
obligations, expenditures, and disbursements. The characters provide the information necessary to enter
transactions into DOD accounting systems.

## TRANSACTION RECORDING

3-116. Finance organizations at all levels of command must ensure financial transactions are accurately
recorded in the Army FMIS. Effective financial data recording is achieved through a joint effort between the
finance community, contracting personnel, and the use of applicable FMIS. Transaction recording must be
timely and accurate to provide relevant account information to the commander.

## TRANSACTION RECONCILIATION

3-117. Transaction reconciliation verifies and corrects fiscal data input into the financial systems of record
supported by appropriate documentation. The budgetary process, from committing funding for a requirement
to disbursing payment for receipt of that requirement, involves numerous individuals with various authorities
and roles. Ideally, a requirement flows through the entire budgetary process without issue; however, errors
do occur and require adjustment. Transaction reconciliation ensures that all transactions in the process
balance and uses supporting documentation as the basis to correct any errors; these processes serve as an
effective internal control system to avoid unmatched, irregular, or erroneous transactions that may result in
illegal payments.

## FINANCIAL STATEMENTS

3-118. With the Chief Financial Officers Act of 1990, Congress mandated that all federal agencies produce
auditable financial statements. Financial statements, through related external audits, should hold finance
organizations accountable for their day-to-day operations. Any financial statements that compile financial
records must use accounting principles and procedures. Commanders use these reports to make resource-
informed decisions.

## COST CAPTURING

3-119. Cost capturing procedures use lines of accounting for both internal and external reporting
requirements. This provides visibility of commitments, obligations, expenditures, disbursements,
reimbursables, and future costs. Reporting procedures should provide accurate information while remaining
simple and flexible. During operations below armed conflict or crisis, HQDA will establish a unique special
program code to capture costs. Additionally, the joint staff shall issue a three-digit Chairman of the Joint
Chiefs of Staff Project Code, which provides precedence for supply requisitions and facilitates cost capturing
and reporting. Each unit that supports operations during crisis or armed conflicts must capture related
obligations and disbursements in its accounting systems at the lowest possible level of the organization. This
provides tracking of obligations and disbursements for affected appropriations. Organizations must use the
**58**
**FM 4-80**
**21 April 2025**
**Finance Operations**
data from existing FMIS to accurately capture cost and not develop cost accounting systems solely for
determining costs for an operation.

## THEATER STRATEGIC-LEVEL ACCOUNTING SUPPORT

3-120. Accounting support during financial disbursements and military expenditures at the theater strategic
level provides real-time financial information that helps commanders make sound resource-based decisions.
3-123. In coordination with the ASA(FM&C) policy, DFAS establishes procedures for accounting, reporting,
and fund management in support of theater strategic level operations. DFAS is the principal DOD
organization for finance and accounting requirements, systems, and functions under the authority and
direction of the USD(C). As such, it provides professional finance and accounting services for DOD
components and other federal agencies. DFAS directs the consolidation, standardization, and integration of
finance and accounting requirements, functions, procedures, operations, and systems, and ensures their
proper relationship with other DOD functional areas (for example, budget, personnel, logistics, acquisition,
and civil engineering).
3-121. USAFMCOM provides oversight and theater strategic level support to accounting operations for all
Army finance organizations. In coordination with the ASA(FM&C), USAFMCOM and the AFMC ensure
the continuity of accounting operations in support of commanders from the strategic to tactical level.
USAFMCOM establishes business process standardization and leads a centralized testing program for
internal controls across all Army business processes, driving the FM enterprise’s ability to effectively conduct
accounting operations.
3-122. The FIOC at the theater level provides coordination between the AFMC and FISC, to complement the
theater accounting policy RM function within supported G-8 staffs and financial units. The focus at the
theater level is on conducting accounting support and internal controls oversight and reporting for the entire
theater.  These activities include the following:
•
Ensure data integrity of collections and disbursements.
•
Reconcile the Analysis of Unmatched Transactions with Treasury deposits.
•
Account for cash and other negotiable instruments.
•
Reconcile accounting and disbursing station number and DSSN transactions with FIBNs (for
example, MAFR).
•
Ensure Collections Information Repository and Payment Information Repository transactions are
accurate.
•
Reconcile Deposit Tickets and Debit Vouchers with Federal Reserve Bank.
•
Assist FIBNs with reconciliation of EagleCash transactions:
3-123. The AFMC, FIOC, and FISC can improve the accounting reporting system by implementing the
Diamond 2 report. This report is a consolidation of all finance data from the various FICOs and FIBNs in
theater. The type of data collected includes casual pays, checks cashed, cash conversions, EagleCash card
activity, paying agent activity, and military pay activity. This data enables the performance of a more accurate
review and trend analysis to provide a common operating picture to the FISC director and G-8 staff. Accuracy
and timeliness in this reporting from the DSSN is important so that it can better reflect on the cash
management section. This report supports theater strategic initiatives by providing a common operating
picture that feeds into the battle update brief and commander update brief

## OPERATIONAL-LEVEL ACCOUNTING SUPPORT

3-124. At the corps level, FM elements have the responsibility to account for funds and expenditures in
accordance with established theater accounting policy. Constant communication with the corps G-8s and
accounting channels facilitates maintaining the accuracy and timeliness of the recorded transactions.
3-125. Accounting support provided by the corps FIBNs, with oversight through the theater finance
organizations, complements the RM function within supported G-8 staffs. The FIBNs provide C2 and
oversight to the FICOs that are operating in the corps or division areas. The FIBNs participate in reviews, as
required, to ensure accounting records are accurate and updated in a timely manner. The FIBN has an internal
controls section that is responsible for providing requested accounting support to operational units in the
corps area. Based on the missions assigned to the corps, the finance accounting functions may include—
**21 April 2025**

**59**
**Chapter 3**
•
Processing deposits to, and payments from, appropriated, deposit, trust, or other special fund
accounts and ensuring disbursements from these accounts are not made without specific authority.
•
Advising the internment facility commander on internment/resettlement operations that relate to pay
and accounting. Upon request, finance units provide training to personnel assigned to the camp or
internment/resettlement unit.

## TACTICAL-LEVEL ACCOUNTING SUPPORT

3-126. To eliminate weaknesses and gaps in financial accounting, is imperative to practice accurate
accounting at the tactical level where expenditures occur and where they are reconciled with official
accounting records. At the tactical level, timely and accurate accounting information enables commanders to
make real time resource-informed decisions.
3-127. At the tactical level, the division G-8 is the principal staff officer responsible for all RM functions and
accounting in support of operations. The division G-8 is the primary interface and technical expert for brigade
S-8s. Depending on mission a FICO is often attached to the division to oversee the employment of financial
platoons and FSTs to provided dispersing, payment support, and accounting oversight for finance operations

### SECTION VI - INTERNAL CONTROLS

3-128. Monitoring and evaluating FM activities could lead to findings that help develop internal controls to
improve operations. Based on the evaluation of progress, leaders and staff personnel make recommendations
to the commander or adjustments within their delegated authority. Assessment diagnoses threats, suggests
improvements to effectiveness, and reveals opportunities. Finance personnel present the assessment results,
their conclusions, and recommendations to the commander.

## OVERVIEW OF INTERNAL CONTROLS

3-129. Finance planners at all echelons will ensure an internal controls process is included as part of each
phase of the finance operations planning process. Internal controls are the procedures, techniques, and devices
employed by managers to mitigate conflicts of interest, fraud, and risk. While audits aim to provide an
external and independent review, internal controls are an organization's self-evaluation. Commanders
establish internal controls and periodic reviews to identify flaws and deficiencies in daily FM business to
reduce the risk of potential loss of funds.
3-130. OMB Circular A-123, applicable DOD instructions, and AR 11-2 prescribe policies and
responsibilities for the Army's Risk Management and Internal Control Program. This program applies to all
Army organizations and programs, reinforces the accountability of Army commanders and managers for
establishing and maintaining effective internal controls tailored to each organization or unit, and provides
greater flexibility in their evaluations of internal controls. FM internal controls provide reasonable assurance
that establishes accountability and control procedures to comply with applicable laws and regulations.
3-131. Constantly evaluating operations, reporting deficiencies, and citing corrective actions is required to
achieve audit readiness. The internal control section may be augmented as required by the AFMC/FISC to
provide a more detailed and robust capability, depending on the mission. Some of the main areas to evaluate
include—
•
Effectiveness and efficiency of operations.
•
Reliability of financial reporting.
•
Compliance with applicable laws and regulations.
**60**
**FM 4-80**
**21 April 2025**
**Finance Operations**
•
Prevention and deterrence of fraud, waste, and abuse.
•
Payment certification.
•
Unprocessed voucher reconciliation.
3-132. Internal control evaluations provide reasonable assurance that established accountability and control
procedures comply with applicable laws and regulations. Reasonable assurance refers to a satisfactory level
of confidence that internal controls are adequate and are operating as intended. Reasonable assurance
recognizes that there are acceptable levels of risk that cannot be avoided because the cost of absolute
assurance would exceed the benefits derived
3-133. As it pertains to finance, the internal control evaluations provide the commanders with a clear picture
that obligations and costs comply with applicable laws, funds are protected, payments are properly disbursed,
and proper accounting is kept of all expenditures (stewardship). It helps FM commanders to promote cost
culture in their immediate area of operations. **Cost culture****is a culture where all leaders and managers**
**factor cost into their decision-making and understand both the near and long-term cost implications**
**of their decisions**. The internal control program must be established as soon as possible, but not at the
expense of operational or tactical considerations.

## ACCURATE ACCOUNTING REPORTING

3-134. The accurate and complete recording of financial transactions within Army FMIS and the review and
reconciliation of these financial transactions ensures the proper expenditure of entrusted funds in support of
operations. Accurate accounting reporting is critical in maintaining successful fiscal responsibility within the
theater of operations.
3-135. Accurate and complete accounting reconciles financial transactions to meet auditability standards.
Accounting outlines the chain of custody of public funds through financial records. Errors in this process
result in discrepancies that can affect commander decision-making. Finance units can identify and reconcile
errors providing more accurate data through two nested functions: transaction reconciliation and financial
statements.

## MAINTAINING SUPPORTING DOCUMENTATION

3-136. Maintaining supporting documentation helps identify, consolidate, and safeguard relevant
transactional documents. The Corporate Electronic Document Management System is the system of record
for military pay documentation. Various regulations provide guidance for documentation retention including
DODI 5015.02 and DOD 7000.14-R Volume 1. The requirement execution process includes many personnel
requiring different supporting documents to complete their portion of the process. The Army has various
systems of record (for example, General Funds Enterprise Business System and Wide Area Workflow
[WAWF]) to embed required supporting documentation to centralize document maintenance. However,
organizations can develop alternate processes to ensure they retain all supporting documentation.

## TRANSACTION RECONCILIATION

3-137. The analysis of unmatched transactions is a tool that provides disbursing officers the ability to evaluate
the accuracy of their disbursing operations. When properly performed, using this tool prevents loss of funds
and prevents fraud. DFAS provides a report by DSSN on a monthly basis that includes DSSN reported deposit
tickets and debit vouchers that do not match the Treasury's report. The discrepancies listed in the report lend
to the accuracy of the disbursing officer's monthly accountability. Immediate action is required to research
and reconcile all unmatched transactions.

## SEPARATION OF DUTIES

3-138. To reduce the risk of error, waste, or wrongful acts, or to reduce the risk of those acts going undetected,
no one individual should control all key aspects of a transaction or event cycle. Rather, duties and
responsibilities (for example, authorizing; approving and recording transactions; making payments;
preparing checks and check payments; certification of funding; reviewing and audition) should be assigned
to separate individuals to ensure that effective checks and balances exist to minimize risk of loss to the
government to the greatest extent possible.
**21 April 2025**
**FM 4-80**
**61**
**Chapter 3**
3-139. Appropriate separation of duties is not always practical or possible due to time constraints, manpower
shortages, or the use of mechanized systems. The commander should be aware of situations where valid,
long-standing separation of duties cannot be achieved, recognize that internal controls have been weakened
as a result of such, and make every effort to compensate for loss of the internal control. Unique situations
resulting in an inability to separate appropriate responsibilities must be reported to the applicable DFAS or
AFMC director or FIBN commander, together with a request for a waiver and recommendations for
compensating for the loss of the internal control.

## SAFEGUARDING FUNDS

3-140. Commanders, along with finance organizations, are responsible for safeguarding funds and protecting
funds from fraud, waste, and abuse. Commanders will control the amount of U.S. and foreign currency
available and used in the area of operations. This is necessary to control black market activities and mitigate
problems related to inflation of either U.S. or HN currency. Finance units must store public funds in
accordance with DOD 7000.14-R, Volume 5 and conduct quarterly cash verifications.

### SECTION VII - FINANCIAL DATA ANALYTICS

3-141. Financial data analytics involves collecting, organizing, and analyzing data in order to produce viable
information that enhances command decision-making ability. Financial data analytics evaluates financial raw
data to drive fact-based, resourced-informed decision making that optimizes commanders' resources.
3-142. Finance units execute numerous transactions, all with various data elements. The ability to draw those
data points from systems of record to identify fiscal trends and develop financial forecasts is key to assisting
commanders in making decisions through a fiscal stewardship lens. Financial data analytics optimizes the
allocation of a commander’s resources, interpreting the data into useful products or reports to inform
operations and provide courses of action. Finance personnel must have a complete understanding of how to
approach and execute data analytics at their specific level of responsibility.
3-143. Financial data analytics involves three actions: decision support, cost capturing, and cost analysis.
The practical application of data analytics across all echelons is exercised using the model of manage,
analyze, visualize, and present.

## FINANCIAL DATA IN DECISION SUPPORT

3-144. Decision support in finance operations focuses on evaluating disbursing and payment support
operations to optimize resources and obtain the greatest effects. Commanders require accurate financial
information to make decisions during operations or on training and maintenance priorities. Decision support
compiles relevant data into a format that allows commanders to understand the information and make optimal
decisions.

## COMMERCIAL VENDOR DATA

3-145. Analyzing commercial vendor data helps the organization establish budgeting and spending goals that
meet the critical demands of the mission. Processing and tailoring these reports in real time enhances the
business decision process by delivering relevant information to commanders as they make financial decisions
involving forecasting, cyclic expenses, and purchasing trends identification.
3-146. The following resources are useful when researching commercial vendors and contractors’ data:
•
Contractor Performance Assessment Reporting System.
•
Federal Awardee Performance and Integrity Information System.
•
Approved HN business advisors.
•
The local embassy.
•
National Counterintelligence and Security Center-Supply Chain Threats.

## PAYING AGENT/MICRO PURCHASE DATA ANALYSIS

3-147. Paying agent and micro purchase analysis benefits commanders, military intelligence, and finance
organizations alike. This analysis can be used to determine trends in types of items bought and vendors used
**62**
**FM 4-80**
**21 April 2025**
**Finance Operations**
and find a nexus between vendors and known illicit activity. Therefore, it is imperative that disbursing
officers capture trends in FOO/paying agent activity and report suspicious activity to upper echelons.

## DATA POLICY AND LEGAL CONSIDERATIONS

3-148. The authorities to collect, store, share, and use identity data and financial information will vary
depending upon the AOR and the partner nations involved. Different countries have strict legal restrictions
on the collection and use of personally identifiable information, resulting in the need for a separate bilateral
or multinational agreement to alleviate partner nation privacy concerns. Due to such legal complexities,
personnel should consult with their SJA or legal advisor along with their corresponding intelligence unit prior
to the collection and use of personally identifiable information or biometric data.

### Chapter 4

## Resource Management

RM constitutes one of FM core competencies and contributes to the Army’s role in national
defense. RM is a critical capability that sources organizations with congressionally approved
resources. This chapter discusses the different processes and tools resource managers use to
fund the force.

### SECTION I – OVERVIEW

4-1. Providing funding support is complex and requires FM professionals to leverage multiple authorizations
and supplemental appropriations that provide additional funding during the fiscal year (FY). A supplemental
funding appropriation is typically in response to urgent and unanticipated operational needs or natural relief
efforts. Commanders and resource managers alike need a thorough understanding of the statutes and
regulations that govern the use of appropriated and non-appropriated funding in order to successfully fund
requirements. Resource managers must understand the flow of funds from Congress to the unit level, the
appropriations/authorization process, and the administrative control of funds while working closely with
fiscal lawyers to ensure compliance with fiscal requirements established by law. **Fund the force****is the**
**critical capability that matches legal and appropriate sources of funds with thoroughly vetted and**
**validated requirements**.
4-2. RM has a unique set of parameters associated with its execution during contingency operations. RM
involves providing financial advice and recommendations to the commander, developing command resource
requirements, identifying sources of funding, determining costs, acquiring funds, distributing and controlling
funds, tracking costs and obligations, capturing costs, conducting reimbursement procedures, accounting and
fiscal validation, and establishing management internal controls.
4-3. Complexities in both the OE and the nature of the mission may require additional flexibility with respect
to the use of fiscal resources by commanders to accomplish their assigned missions. Operating with
multinational partners may necessitate providing logistics or other support to their forces beyond what a
current acquisition and cross-servicing agreement (ACSA) can provide. ACSA is a formal agreement
between the DOD and other countries or international organizations that allows for the exchange of supplies,
services, and logistic support. However, there must be specific legal authorities that allow the expenditure of
appropriated funds to provide for that support. Whenever there is no clear statutory authority, the SJA should
be consulted. Statutory limitations on spending certain types of appropriations to satisfy unforeseen
requirements could restrict the commander's ability to legally apply fiscal resources toward the successful
execution of a mission. In some instances, the requirement may be of such a unique nature that no existing
fiscal authority provides legal means to satisfy it. In all these cases, legislative relief of some kind may be
necessary to provide commanders with the requisite fiscal flexibility to fund emergent requirements that fall
outside the bounds of existing fiscal law.
4-4. Resource managers at all levels must be aware of extraordinary measures, including emergency funding
authorities, that may be used to incur obligations in excess or advance of available appropriations. A thorough
understanding of sources and authorities can provide resource managers with a means of remaining within
the limits of the law and a method to develop alternative funding options.

## THEATER OPENING

4-5. As part of RM operations conducted during mobilization and pre-deployment, resource managers
should—
•
Deploy as a member of the predeployment site survey team.
•
Provide RM advice and assistance.

## THEATER CLOSING

4-6. Reconciling key activities during theater closing could be challenging due to remote locations of units

Reconcile contract payments made.

Reconcile all unmatched transactions.

Reconcile all types of funding by performing joint reviews.

Reconcile prior year funding.

4-7. Only the Treasury may close a DSSN. USAFMCOM coordinates and synchronizes with enterprise-level
financial operations and unified action partners (DFAS, Federal Reserve Bank) to provide technical
coordination to finance units and commands across the theater for requirements to deactivate or close a
DSSN.

•
Closing out all contracts and obligations.
•
Requesting additional obligation authority to replace or repair damaged or destroyed equipment.

Settling outstanding ACSA requirements/reimbursements.
